## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science - thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task seeks a constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature. In materials science, stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic behavior and on temperature through thermal softening, thermal activation, and temperature-dependent elastic moduli.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (strain hardening with power-law thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Arrhenius thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential thermal softening with hardening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear with saturation)
- Polynomial thermal dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T + c5 * T**2) (quadratic temperature dependence)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart type creep law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear stress-strain at small strains transitioning to sublinear at large strains → power-law epsilon**c with c<1 or saturating forms like 1-exp(-c*epsilon)
- Thermal softening that vanishes at a melting point → homologous temperature factor (c0 - c1*T) or (1 - c0*T**c1) that goes to zero
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → multiplicative separation sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) where g(T) is decreasing
- Thermally activated processes (creep, dislocation glide) → Arrhenius-type exp(-c/T) or exp(c*T) temperature dependence
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational forms epsilon/(epsilon + c)
- Yield stress offset (elastic-plastic transition) → additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) representing initial yield
- Competing hardening and recovery mechanisms → difference of power laws or exponentials: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*epsilon**c3
- Nonlinear coupling between strain and temperature → product terms epsilon**c1 * T**c2 or epsilon * exp(c*T)

c7*exp(T**2*c8)"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)
```

With c2 = c5 = c8 = 316.1945..., let me call this value K.

Expanding:
```
c0*epsilon*(-c1*T + c1*K + c3) - c4*T + c4*K + c7*epsilon**c6*T - c7*epsilon**c6*K
```

Grouping by terms:
- **T*epsilon**: -c0*c1 = -31.12 * 0.05295 ≈ -1.6479
- **epsilon** (constant part): c0*(c1*K + c3) = 31.12*(0.05295*316.19 + 1) = 31.12*(16.743 + 1) = 31.12*17.743 ≈ 552.17
- **T**: -c4 + c7*epsilon**c6... wait, let me be more careful.

Let me re-expand:
```
= -c0*c1*T*epsilon + c0*(c1*K + c3)*epsilon - c4*T + c4*K + c7*T*epsilon**c6 - c7*K*epsilon**c6
```

So the GT has these basis function terms:
1. **T*epsilon**: coefficient = -c0*c1
2. **epsilon**: coefficient = c0*(c1*K + c3)
3. **T**: coefficient = -c4
4. **constant (1)**: coefficient = c4*K
5. **T*epsilon^c6**: coefficient = c7
6. **epsilon^c6**: coefficient = -c7*K

Where c6 ≈ 0.5976 (not 0, 1, or 2 — a fractional power).

So the GT is a linear combination of: {T*epsilon, epsilon, T, 1, T*epsilon^c6, epsilon^c6}

**Key constraint**: The coefficients of the constant term and T term are related (both involve c4 and K), and similarly the coefficients of T*epsilon^c6 and epsilon^c6 are related (both involve c7 and K). But since candidate constants are FREE, these constraints don't matter — we just need the right basis functions.

So I need candidates that have exactly these 6 basis functions (or can reduce to them): **T*epsilon, epsilon, T, 1, T*epsilon^c6, epsilon^c6** where c6 is a free fractional exponent.

Let me now check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6 + c7*epsilon**c3 + c8*epsilon

Basis: {T*epsilon, T, T*epsilon^c3, epsilon^c5, 1, epsilon^c3, epsilon}

This has T*epsilon^c3 and epsilon^c3 (good, maps to c6 power), plus epsilon^c5 as an extra term. The GT doesn't have an independent epsilon^c5 term unless c5 = c3 (then it merges with epsilon^c3) or c5 = 1 (merges with epsilon). Since constants are free, we can set c5 = c3 or c5 = 1. Yes! Setting c5 = 1 makes epsilon^c5 = epsilon, which merges with c8*epsilon. Or setting c5 = c3 merges with c7*epsilon^c3.

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: T**2*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2 + T*c3*epsilon**c4 + c5 + c6*epsilon**c4 + c7*epsilon

Has T**2 term. Set c0 = 0 to eliminate. Then: {T*epsilon, T, T*epsilon^c4, 1, epsilon^c4, epsilon}. This matches exactly!

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**
